APPENDIX   T. 


Pleadings  in  Snits  brought  against  the  Committee  on  VolunteeriDg, 


Vol.  II.— 2 


19  Doc.  No.  12. 


Case  of  John  McHugh. 


Complaint. 

SUPKEME  COURT— KINGS  COUNTY. 


John  McIIugh,  by  his  Attorney  in 
fact,  Mary  McHugfi, 

against 

Orison  Blunt,  Chairman  of  the  New| 
York  County  Volunteer  Commit- 
tee. 

The  complaint  of  the  plaintiff  respectfully  shows  to  this 
Court  that  the  said  Orison  Blunt,  in  his  official  capacity  as 
chairman  of  said  committee,  was  duly  authorized  by  the 
Board  of  Supervisors  of  the  County  of  New  York,  in  the 
month  of  November,  1S63,  to  pay  to  each  of  the  veterans  of 
the  volunteers  of  the  State  of  New  York  in  the  service  of 
the  United  States,  re-enlisting  in  said  service  and  credited 
as  part  of  the  quota  of  the  said  County  of  New  York 
under  the  late  calls  of  the  President  of  the  United  States 
in  18G3  for  three  hundred  thousand  and  two  hundred  thou- 


Doc.  No.  12,  20 

sand  men,  the  sum  of  three  hundred  dollars ;  that  the  said 
John  McHugh  was,  on  the  2Sth  day  of  January,  1S64,  a 
veteran  private,  of  Captain  Charles  Morrison's  Company 
(B)  Fourth  Kegiment  Heavy  Artillery,  New  York  Volun- 
teers ;  that  on  the  28th  day  of  December,  1863,  at  Fort 
Ethan  Allen,  Virginia,  by  reason  of  his  re-enlistment  as  a 
veteran,  he  was  discharged,  with  a  furlough  for  thirty 
days;  that  he  resides  in  the  City  of  Brooklyn,  and  returned 
from  Virginia  to  this  place,  where  he  remained  to  within 
a  day  or  two  of  the  expiration  of  his  said  furlough,  so  that 
he  was  compelled  to  return  to  his  said  Company  before  he 
could  ascertain  from  the  muster-in  officer  to  which  County 
he  was  credited,  and  without  having  received  his  bounty 
aforesaid  ;  that  afterward  information  from  Captain  W.Van 
Horn,  the  muster-in  officer,  was  received,  stating  that 
plaintiff  was  credited  to  the  County  of  New  York  as  one 
of  its  quota ;  that  thereupon  the  said  John  McHugh,  being 
engaged  with  his  Company  in  actual  service,  and  unable 
for  that  reason  to  get  another  furlough  or  to  make  per- 
sonal application  to  the  defendant  for  his  bounty,  made 
and  executed  a  power  of  attorney  to  his  wife,  Mary  Mc- 
Hugh, on  the  20th  day  of  April,  1864,  in  the  presence  of 
"William  II.  Burt,  Lieutenant  commanding  said  Company 
B,  and  acknowledged  before  the  Adjutant  of  said  regiment 
on  the  same  day  (20th  April),  authorizing  her  to  receive 
for  him  said  bounty  of  three  hundred  dollars. 

That  on  or  about  the  5th  day  of  May,  1864,  Captain 


21  Doc.  No.  1:2. 

Charles  Morrison,  of  said  city,  commanding  said  Company, 
made  an  affidavit  as  to  the  identity  of  said  John  McHugh 
and  Mary  his  wife  and  the  Adjutant  of  his  regiment ;  that 
the  funds  for  the  payment  of  said  bounties  having  been 
furnished  to  said  Blunt  by  the  Board  of  Supervisors  afore- 
said ;  that  in  pursuance  of  said  power  of  attorney  given 
as  aforesaid,  with  that  and  all  of  the  said  papers  before 
referred  to,  on  or  about  the  Tth  day  of  May,  186-±,  plain- 
tiff's said  wife  called  on  the  said  Orison  Blunt,  at  his  office 
for  the  payment  of  said  bounties,  at  the  corner  of  Cham- 
bers street  and  Broadway,  in  the  City  of  New  York,  and 
there  exhibited  all  of  said  papers  before  referred  to  to 
him,  and  demanded  of  him  the  bounty  due  and  coming  to 
her  said  husband,  amounting  to  three  hundred  dollars; 
that  thereupon  the  said  defendant,  in  an  insulting  and 
contemptuous  manner  refused  to  pay  the  same ;  where- 
fore, said  defendant  became  indebted  to  the  said  plaintiff 
in  the  said  sum  of  three  hundred  dollars,  for  which  sum 
he  demands  judgment  against  said  defendant,  besides  the 
costs  and  expenses  of  this  action. 

C.J.JACK,

29  Doc.  No.  12. 


"A." 
AN  ORDINANCE 

TO  PROVIDE  FOR  THE  PROCUREMENT  OF  SUBSTITUTES  FOR 
DRAFTED  SOLDIERS  FOR  THE  ARMIES  OF  THE  UNION,  PRO- 
VIDED THE  SAME  CAN  BE  COUNTED  AND  ALLOWED  ON  THE 
QUOTA  OF  THE  CITY  AND  COUNTY  OF  NEW  YORK  IN  ANY 
FUTURE  DRAFT. 

The  Board  of  Supervisors  of  the  County  of  New  York  do 
01  dain  asfolloics  : 

Section  1.  In  order  to  prevent  the  withdrawal  from  the 
County  of  any  considerable  number  of  active,  able-bodied 
citizens,  whose  presence  and  services  are  deemed  neces- 
sary for  the  maintenance  of  public  order  and  the  security  of 
its  inhabitants,  and  who  may  hereafter  be  drafted  to  serve 
as  soldiers  in  the  armies  of  the  Union,  and  for  the  pur- 
pose of  expediting  the  raising  of  the  additional  num- 
ber of  men  recently  called  for  by  the  President  of  the 
United  States,  the  Comptroller  is  hereby  authorized  and 
directed  to  pay,  as  hereinafter  provided,  such  sum  and 
sums  of  money  as  may  be  necessary  to  obtain  acceptable 
substitutes  for  such  service,  not  exceeding  three  hundred 
dollars  for  any  one  substitute,  who  shall  be  credited  and 
allowed  on  account  of  the  quota  of  men  required  to  be 
furnished  by  this  County  under  any  future  draft  ordered 
by  the  President  of  the  United  States. 


Doc.  No.  12.  30 

Sec  2.  The  moneys  authorized  by  the  preceding  section 
to  be  paid  for  substitutes  shall  be  paid  to  such  substitutes 
respectively,  or  their  duly  authorized  agents,  at  the  office 
of  the  Comptroller,  or  suth  other  place  or  places  as  said 
Comptroller  may  designate,  immediately  on  their  furnish- 
ing him  with  satisfactory  evidence  of  their  having  enlisted 
and  been  duly  accepted  and  mustered  into  the  military 
service  of  the  United  States  for  the  term  of  three  years  or 
during  the  war. 

Sec  3.  The  Mayor  and  Comptroller  of  the  City  of  New 
York  and  the  following-named  members  of  this  Board, 
that  is  to  say,  Elijah  F.  Purdy,  Orison  Blunt,  William  M. 
Tweed,  and  William  R.  Stewart,  are  hereby  designated 
and  appointed  a  committee  to  procure  the  enlistment  of 
the  substitutes  authorized  by  this  ordinance,  provided  the 
Government  will  allow  the  number  of  men  so  procured 
to  be  credited  and  deducted  from  the  quota  of  this  County 
in  any  future  draft. 

Sec  4.  In  order  that  the  Comptroller  may  be  enabled 
to  make  the  payments  hereinbefore  authorized  and  the 
expenses  necessarily  incurred  in  the  execution  of  this  or- 
dinance, he  is  hereby  authorized  to  borrow,  from  time  to 
time,  on  the  faith  and  credit  of  the  County  of  New  York, 
a  sum  not  exceeding  an  aggregate  of  two  million  dollars 
(§2,000,000),  which  amount  is  hereby  appropriated  there- 
for. 


31  Doc.  No.  12. 

Sec.  5.  The  money  so  borrowed  shall  be  deposited  in 
the  County  treasury  by  the  persons  lending  the  same,  and 
the  County  Treasurer  shall  give  proper  receipts  therefor. 
On  presenting  such  receipts  to  the  Comptroller,  the  lend- 
ers of  the  money  shall  be  entitled  to  receive  bonds  of  the 
County  of  New  York  for  an  equal  amount,  which  shall  be 
designated  and  known  as  "  Soldiers'  Substitute  Bounty 
Fund  Bonds,"  and  be  prepared  and  signed  by  the  Comp- 
troller, countersigned  by  the  Mayor,  and  sealed  with  the 
common  seal  of  this  Board,  attested  by  the  Clerk. 

Sec.  6.  The  said  bonds  shall  bear  interest  at  such  rate 
as  may  be  agreed  upon,  not  exceeding  six  per  cent,  per 
annum,  and  the  principal  thereof  shall  be  redeemable  on 
or  before  the  1st  day  of  June,  1861.  The  faith  of  the 
County  of  New  York  and  of  the  Board  of  Supervisors  of 
said  County  is  hereby  solemnly  pledged  for  the  payment 
and  redemption  of  said  bonds  and  the  interest  thereon, 
according  to  their  tenor. 

Sec.  7.  The  Comptroller  is  hereby  further  authorized 
to  cause  a  transfer  to  be  made  to  the  credit  of  the  Soldiers' 
Substitute  Bounty  Fund,  hereby  created,  of  the  amount 
remaining  unexpended  after  all  expenses  are  paid  and  the 
accounts  are  fully  closed,  of  the  moneys  appropriated  and 
borrowed  in  pursuance  of  the  ordinance  entitled  "  An 
ordinance  to  provide  for  the  procurement  of  substitutes 
for  certain  citizens  of  the  City  and  County  of  New  York 


Doc.  No.  12.  32 

who  have  been  or  may  hereafter  be  drafted  to  serve  in 
the  army  of  the  Union  daring  the  existing  war,  and  for 
other  purposes,"  passed  August  28, 1803,  and  the  amount 
so  transferred  may  be  used  and  paid  for  the  procurement 
of  substitutes  as  authorized  and  provided  by  this  ordinance. 


KE-ENLISTED  MEN— NOTICE. 

Re-enlisted  men  claiming  the  New  York  bounty  of 
three  hundred  dollars  (8300),  whose  original  term  of  ser- 
vice would  have  expired  within  the  year  1864,  and  who 
have  so  re-enlisted  since  the  17th  of  November,  1863,  are 
required  to  appear  before  the  committee  in  person  with  the 
following  papers : 

First — Their  discharge. 

Second — A  muster-in  roll,  certified  by  the  Commissary 
of  Musters,  showing  that  the  men  are  credited  to  the  City 
and  County  of  New  York. 

The  Congressional  Districts  of  New  York  City  and 
County  are  the  Fourth,  Fifth,  Sixth,  Seventh,  Eighth,  and 
Ninth.  The  muster-in  rolls  will  be  retained  by  the  com- 
mittee.

Complaint. 

SUPREME  COURT— KINGS  COUNTY: 

James    Morgan 

against 
Orison  Blunt. 


The  complaint  of  the  above-named  plaintiff  respectfully 
shows  to  this  Court — 

That  at  the  City  and  County  of  New  York,  on  or  about 
the  16th  day  of  August,  1804,  and  during  the  period  of 
the  alleged  transactions  hereinafter  mentioned,  the  above- 
named  defendant  was  chairman  of  the  New  York  County 
Committee  on  Volunteering,  and  also  recruiting  officer 
for  the  enlistment  and  shipping  of  recruits  in  the  navy, 
for  the  purpose  of  filling  the  quotas  in  the  several  Con- 
gressional Districts  in  the  City  and  County  of  New  York, 
under  the  different  calls  of  the  President  of  the  United 
States. 

That  at  the  City  and  County  of  New  York,  on  the  16th 
day  of  August,  1864,  the  plaintiff  applied  to  the  defend- 
ant, stating  that  he  desired  to  enlist  in  the  United  States 


35  Doc.  No.  12. 

navy  as  a  volunteer,  and  not  otherwise ;  and  it  was  then 
and  there  agreed  to  and  between  the  said  plaintiff  and  the 
defendant  that  lie,  the  said  plaintiff,  was  to  ship  as  a  volun- 
teer for  the  period  of  one  year  from  the  date  of  said  en- 
listment ;  and  it  was  further  agreed  that  he,  said  plaintiff, 
should  receive  as  consideration  for  said  enlisting  the  sum 
of  two  hundred  and  seventy-five  dollars  as  a  volunteer 
bounty  from  the  City  and  County  of  New  York  when 
he  enlisted,  and  the  further  sum  of  one  hundred  dollars 
bounty  from  the  United  States  Government  when  he  was 
delivered  on  the*  United  States  receiving-ship,  making  a 
sum  total  of  three  hundred  and  seventy-five  dollars. 

That  said  plaintiff,  relying  on  said  representations  and 
agreement,  was  thereby  induced  to  enlist,  and  was  placed 
on  the  United  States  receiving-ship  Vermont,  lying  at  the 
Brooklyn  Navy-yard,  at  which  time  and  place  he  was 
paid  the  sum  of  two  hundred  and  seventy  dollars  by  said 
defendant,  or  his  agent,  and  was  then  informed  that  he 
would  receive  the  further  sum  of  one  hundred  dollars 
from  the  Paymaster  of  the  receiving-ship. 

That  plaintiff  has  repeatedly  demanded  of  the  said  Pay- 
master the  said  sum  of  one  hundred  dollars,  but  has  been 
informed  that  he  is  not  entitled  to  the  said  Government 
bounty  for  the  reason  that  he  was  enlisted  as  a  substitute. 

That  the  said  defendant,  at  the  time  of  said  agreement 


Doc.  No.  12.  36 

to  enlist  as  aforesaid,  offered  and  did  try  to  induce  the 
said  plaintiff  to  enlist  in  the  naval  service  as  aforesaid  as 
a  substitute,  and  for  which  the  plaintiff  could  have  ob- 
tained for  so  enlisting  as  a  substitute  the  sum  of  live  hun- 
dred dollars,  but  that  said  plaintiff  positively  refused  and 
declined  to  enlist  as  a  substitute. 

That  on  the  said  16th  day  of  August,  1SG4,  at  the  said 
City  and  County  of  New  York,  the  said  defendant,  with 
intent  to  deceive  and  defraud  the  plaintiff,  did  enlist  said 
plaintiff  in  the  United  States  navy  as  a  substitute,  at  the 
same  time  falsely  and  fraudulently  representing  that  he 
had  shipped  in  the  navy  as  a  volunteer. 

That  said  plaintiff,  at  the  time  of  said  enlistment,  signed 
shipping  articles  purporting  to  be  volunteer  enlistment 
papers,  which  were  not  read  or  explained  to  him  before 
signing,  and  plaintiff  is  unable  to  state  what  they  contained. 

That  plaintiff  had  shipped  as  a  volunteer,  and  had  no 
intention  and  did  not  ship  as  a  substitute. 

That  said  plaintiff  is  informed  and  alleges  the  fact  to  be 
that  said  defendant,  contrary  to  the  agreement  aforesaid 
made  and  contrary  to  the  representations  aforesaid,  did, 
on  or  about  the  lGth  day  of  August,  1864,  with  intent  to 
deceive  and  defraud  this  plaintiff,  and  against  his  will 
and  unknown  to  him,  make  out  and  alter  said  enlistment 
papers,  and  did  then  sell  said  papers  to  one  Frederick  P. 


37  Doc.  No.  12. 

Elliott,  of  the  City,  County  and  State  of  New  York,  for  a 
large  sum,  to  wit,  about  seven  hundred  dollars,  thereby 
placing  said  plaintiff  in  the  navy  as  a  substitute  for  said 
Elliott. 

That  said  representations  were  false  and  untrue,  and 
were  made  expressly  for  the  purpose  of  defrauding  this 
plaintiff,  as  the  defendant  well  knew  at  the  time. 

That  by  reason  of  the  promises  and  the  false  represen- 
tations aforesaid  made,  this  plaintiff  was  misled  to  his 
damage  in  the  sum  of  seven  hundred  dollars  ($700),  for 
which  sum,  less  the  sum  of  two  hundred  and  seventy  dol- 
lars ($270)  received  at  the  time  of  enlisting,  the  plaintiff 
demands  judgment  against  the  said  defendant,  besides  tho 
costs  and  disbursements  of  this  action. 

THOMAS  C.  BOWEN,

NEW  YORK  SUPREME  COURT— COUNTY  OF 

KINGS. 


James  Morgan 

agsl. 
Orison  Blunt. 


The  answer  of  the  defendant  to  the  complaint  herein, 
respectfully  shows  to  the  Court : 

First — That  he  admits  that  at  the  times  mentioned  in 
the  complaint  he  was  chairman  of  the  County  Volunteer 
Committee  of  the  County  of  New  York,  and  he  alleges 
that  at  said  time  the  said  committee  was  intrusted  with 
the  power  and  duty  of  procuring  volunteers  for  the  army 
and  navy  of  the  United  States,  to  fill  the  quota  assigned 


39  Doc.  No.  12. 

to  the  said  County  and  the  various  Congressional  Districts 
thereof;  and  that  this  defendant,  as  such  chairman,  had, 
at  or  before  said  period,  received  from  one  Frederick  B. 
Elliott  the  sum  of  two  hundred  and  seventy  dollars,  for 
the  purpose  of  procuring  a  substitute  who  would  enlist  in 
his  behalf  in  the  navy  of  the  United  States  for  the  term 
of  one  year,  and  then  held  the  same  for  that  purpose. 

But  this  defendant  denies  that  he  was  a  recruiting  offi- 
cer for  the  enlisting  or  shipping  of  recruits,  as  in  the  said 
complaint  mentioned. 

Second — This  defendant  denies  that  he  ever  made  the 
false  or  fraudulent  representations  to  the  plaintiff  alleged 
in  the  complaint,  or  any  false  or  fraudulent  representa- 
tions or  statements  whatever. 

Third — This  defendant  denies  that  he  ever  made  the 
agreement  with  the  said  plaintiff  which  is  alleged  in  the 
complaint,  or  that  it  was  ever  agreed  between  the  said 
plaintiff  and  defendant  that  the  said  plaintiff  should  ship 
as  a  volunteer  in  the  navy  of  the  United  States  for  the 
period  mentioned  in  the  said  complaint,  or  otherwise,  or 
that  it  was  agreed  between  them  that  the  said  plaintiff 
should  ship  as  such  volunteer  in  any  manner  whatever, 
or  that  the  said  plaintiff  should  receive,  in  consideration 
of  enlisting  as  such  volunteer,  the  sum  mentioned  in  the 
said  complaint,  or  any  sum  whatever ;  or  that  the  said 
plaintiff,  relying  on  any  such  representations,  statements, 


Doc.  No.  12.  40 

or  agreements  as  are  mentioned  in  the  complaint,  was 
placed  upon  the  receiving-ship  Vermont,  mentioned  in  the 
complaint,  or  that  any  such  information  was  communi- 
cated by  the  defendant  to  the  plaintiff  on  being  received 
on  said  ship,  as  is  mentioned  in  said  complaint. 

And  he  also  denies  that  any  person  on  board  who  re- 
ceived the  said  plaintiff  was  the  agent  of  this  defendant. 

And  he  denies,  upon  information  and  belief,  that  any 
such  information  was  communicated  or  any  such  statement 
was  made  to  the  said  plaintiff  upon  his  being  received 
upon  said  ship,  as  is  stated  and  alleged  in  said  complaint, 
or  otherwise. 

Fourth — This  defendant  also  denies  that,  with  the  intent 
in  the  complaint  mentioned,  or  otherwise,  he  enlisted  the 
said  plaintiff  in  the  United  States  navy  as  a  substitute,  or 
that  he  falsely  or  fraudulently  represented  that  the  said 
plaintiff  had  enlisted  as  volunteer ;  and  he  further  denies 
that  the  said  plaintiff  ever  declined  to  enlist  as  a  substi- 
tute, or  that  this  defendant  enlisted  said  plaintiff  in  any 
manner  whatever. 

Fifth — This  defendant  has  no  knowledge  or  information 
sufficient  to  form  a  belief  as  to  whether  the  said  plaintiff 
made  the  demand  on  Paymaster  mentioned  in  the  com- 
plaint fur  the  sum  therein  mentioned,  or  for  any  sum 
whatever. 


41  Doc.  No.  12. 

Sixth — This  defendant  denies  that  he  is  indebted  to  the 
plaintiff  in  the  sum  mentioned  in  the  complaint,  or  in  any 
sum  whatever;  and  he  farther  alleges  that  he  has  no 
knowledge  or  information  sufficient  to  form  a  belief  as  to 
whether  the  plaintiff  could  have  obtained  the  sum  men- 
tioned in  the  complaint  as  a  substitute,  but  he  avers  that 
he  could  not  have  obtained  that  sum  from  the  County  of 
New  York. 

Seventh — This  defendant  denies  that,  with  the  intent 
mentioned  in  the  complaint,  or  otherwise,  he  made  out  or 
altered  the  enlistment  papers  of  the  plaintiff,  as  in  the  com- 
plaint mentioned  or  otherwise,  or  with  such  intent  or 
otherwise  did  sell  the  same  to  Frederick  B.  Elliot,  therein 
mentioned,  for  the  sum  therein  mentioned,  or  any  sum 
whatever,  or  had  anything  whatever  to  do  with  said 
papers.

other  allegation  in  said  complaint  contained  not  heretofore 
admitted  or  denied,  except  as  hereinafter  stated.

the  Court  that  at  or  about  the  time  in  said  complaint 
mentioned  the  said  plaintiff  applied  to  the  said  defendant, 
who  was  then  chairman  of  the  County  Volunteer  Com- 
mittee, as  before  stated,  for  the  purpose  of  being  enlisted 
into  the  naval  service  of  the  United  States  as  a  substitute 
for  persons  liable  to  be  drafted,  as  aforesaid  ;  that  it  was 


Doc.  No.  12.  42 

then  and  there  distinctly  and  expressly  stated  by  the  said 
plaintiff  that  he  was  an  alien,  and  was  not  liable  to  such 
draft;  that  the  said  plaintiff  was  informed  that  he  could 
and  would  be  received  as  a  substitute  into  the  navy  of  the 
United  States,  and  that  as  such  substitute  he  would  be 
entitled  on  enlisting  for  one  year  to  receive  the  sum  of 
two  hundred  and  seventy  dollars,  which  included  hand-

would  be  paid  to  him  upon  his  having  passed  the  final  ex-

ment appointed  for  that  purpose,  and  on  being  received  on 
board  the  United  States  receiving-ship  Vermont,  then 
lying  at  the  Navy-yard  in  Brooklyn.

two  hundred  and  seventy  dollars  was  all  the  bounty  and

hand-money  then  allowed  and  paid  by  the  said  committee

The  plaintiff  complains  of  the  defendant  as  follows: 

First — That  in  and  during  the  month  of  February,

the  County  of  New  York,  and  was  the  disbursing  officer 
of  such  committee,  and  intrusted  with  the  making  of  the 
payments  hereinafter  set  forth.

1865,  the  said  committee  caused  to  be  printed  and  pub- 
lished in  divers  newspapers  published  in  the  City  and 
County  of  New  York,  and  to  be  circulated  and  given  out  to 
the  public,  an  advertisement,  of  which  a  copy  is  hereto  an- 
nexed, marked  "  Schedule  A  ;"  and  that  the  said  committee 
also  caused  to  be  printed  and  distributed  to  the  several 
mustering  officers  of  the  United  States  in  the  said  City

unto annexed,  marked  "Schedule  B,"  to  be  signed  by  said 
mustering  officers,  upon  every  enlistment  of  a  recruit  to

SCHEDULE  A. 

(Referred  to  in  the  foregoing  complaint.) 


THE   QUOTA   OF  NEW  YORK. 

FIFTEEN   THOUSAND   VOLUNTEERS   WANTED    FOR    NEW    YORK 

COUNTY. 

Increased  Bounties  and  Hand-money. 

At  a  meeting  of  the  County  Committee  on  Volunteer- 
ing, held  on  Saturday,  February  1,  1S65 — 

Present:  Orison  Blunt,  Esq.,  Chairman;  Hon.  M.  T. 
Brennan,  Comptroller ;  Hon.  Elijah  F.  Purdy,  Supervisor ; 
Hon.  William  M.  Tweed,  Supervisor;  Hon.  William  H. 
Stewart,  Supervisor. 

On  motion  of  Supervisor  William  M.  Tweed,  it  was 
unanimously  resolved  that  the  County  pay —

bounty,  and  one  hundred  dollars  ($100)  hand-monoy.

APPENDIX    U. 


Eeport  of  the  Select  Committee  of  the  House  of  Kepresentatives  rela- 
tive to  Beimbursing  the  Loyal  States  for  Expenditures  for  the 
War. 


WAR  DEBTS  OF  THE  LOYAL  STATES. 


In  House  of  Representatives. 

Mr.  Blaine,  from  the  Select  Committee  on  the  "War 
Debts  of  the  Loyal  States,  made  the  following  report : 

The  select  committee  to  whom  was  referred,  on  the  11th 
of  December  last,  a  bill  "  to  reimburse  the  loyal  States 
for  advances  made  and  debts  contracted  in  support  of 
the  war  for  the  preservation  of  the  Union,"  ask  leave  to 
report  the  same  in  an  amended  form,  which  is  herewith 
submitted. 

Immediately  after  being  appointed,  the  committee  re- 
solved to  ascertain,  in  an  authentic  manner,  the  amount 
expended  in  support  of  the  war  by  each  State,  and  by 
the  counties,  cities,  and  towns  within  each  State.  To 
this  end,  a  letter  of  inquiry  was  addressed  to  the  several 
Governors,  and  responses,  giving  the  desired  information 
have  been  received  from  every  State  except  California, 
Oregon,  and  Nevada.  Answers  by  mail  are  scarcely  due 
from  those  distant  States,  but  the  committee  have  not 

deemed  it  important  to  delay  their  report  in  order  to  hear 
Vol.  II.— 5 


Doc.  No.  12.  66 

from  them,  inasmuch  as  their  slight  participation  in  the 
war  renders  it  certain  that  their  expenditures  could  not 
be  sufficiently  largo  to  have  an  appreciable  influence 
upon  the  measure  v/nich  the  committee  ask  leave  to 
propose. 

The  following  table  will  show  the  amounts  returned  by 
the  several  States,  as  expended  directly  by  the  States,  or 
by  the  municipal  corporations  within  the  States.  The 
sum  total  reaches  the  enormous  amount  of  four  hundred 
and  sixty-seven  million  nine  hundred  and  fifty-four  thou- 
sand three  hundred  and  sixty-four  dollars  ($467,954,364). 
In  many  instances  the  Governors,  in  communicating  the 
statistics,  have  advised  the  committee  that  for  want  of 
exact  data  they  were  compelled  to  make  estimates,  and 
that  these  estimates  were  believed  to  be  always  under 
rather  than  over  the  truth.  Had  the  time  been  more  ex- 
tended, and  the  accounts  made  up  in  all  cases  with  more 
precision,  there  can  bo  no  doubt  that  the  aggregate 
would  have  reached /bzr/*  hundred  and  seventy-five  millions, 
if  it  did  not  indeed  greatly  exceed  that  sum.  And  it 
must  be  remembered  that  this  does  not  include  the 
amount  raised  by  State  taxation  for  war  expenses,  nor 
any  of  that  vast  sum  so  generously  contributed  through- 
out the  loyal. States  by  individuals  and  by  associations 
for  the  support  of  the  Union  cause.  It  simply  includes 
the  amounts  that  State  and  municipal  authorities  raised 
by  loans — a  very  large  proportion  of  which  is  still  un- 


67  Doc.  No.  12. 

pakl,  and  demands  the  severest  form  of  taxation  to  pro- 
vide for  its  annual  interest.  With  this  explanation,  the 
following  table  of  State  and  local  expenditure  will  be  the 
more  clearly  understood: 

Maine $12,632,580 

New  Hampshire 13,125,000

)-iv) 


Minnesota 2,518,361

Kansas 818,000 


Doc.  No.  12  68 

Simultaneously  with  this  call  upon  the  States  for  in- 
formation in  regard  to  their  expenditures,  the  committee, 
by  a  resolution  of  the  House,  obtained  from  the  Secretary 
of  War  a  statement  of  the  number  of  troops  furnished 
by  eacli  State  under  the  several  calls  during  the  war,  to- 
gether with  an  exhibit  of  the  aggregate  from  each  of  the 
States  reduced  to  a  uniform  standard  of  three-years 
service.  The  tabular  statement  of  the  Provost-Marshal 
General,  giving  this  information,  is  appended  to  this 
report,  and  it  will  be  seen  that  the  total  number  of 
three-years  men  for  the  war  was  two  million  one  hun- 
dred and  fifty-four  thousand  three  hundred  and  eleven 
(2,154,311). 

Without  entering  into  any  calculation  as  to  the  dif- 
ferent ratio  of  expense  in  raising  troops  in  different 
States,  it  will  be  observed  that  the  average  for  all  the 
States  exhibits  the  fact  that  each  three-years  man  that 
entered  the  United  States  service  during  the  war  cost 
about  two  hundred  and  twenty  dollars  besides  the  amount 
paid  by  the  General  Government.  It  is  not  the  province 
of  the  committee  to  inquire  whether  this  expenditure  was 
in  all  cases  wisely  made.  It  is  sufficient  to  state  that 
it  was  actually  incurred  under  what  was  believed  to 
be  the  pressing  and  imperious  necessity  of  the  Union 
cause. 

In  the  judgment  of  the  committee,  it  would  not  be  fair 


GO  Doc.  No.  12. 

and.  equitable  to  propose  any  mode  of  reimbursement  to 
the  several  States,  except  that  which  is  based  on  the  num- 
ber of  men  furnished  by  each  during  the  war.  All  the 
States  were  under  precisely  the  same  obligation  to  respond 
to  the  call  of  the  Government,  in  proportion  to  their  re- 
spective numbers  of  enrolled  men-,  and  the  committee 
have  not  therefore  felt  at  liberty  to  make  any  discrimina- 
tion in  favor  of  one  State  over  another  in  consequence  of 
the  different  cost  in  filling  their  quotas.  Local  expendi- 
ture was,  indeed,  a  recognized  necessity  in  all  the  States, 
and  strict  justice  will  be  maintained  by  making  an  im- 
partial reimbursement,  exactly  proportioned  to  the  aid 
which  each  State  rendered  to  the  common  cause  of  the 
Union. 

The  committee,  for  the  most  obvious  reasons,  have  not 
considered  it  expedient  to  attempt  a  system  of  reimburse- 
ment sufficiently  comprehensive  to  include  the  total  outlay 
within  the  States.  The  burden  which  would  thus  be  pre- 
cipitated on  the  General  Government  would  be  too  heavy, 
and  might  end  in  oppressing  instead  of  relieving  the  dif- 
ferent members  of  the  Union,  by  impairing  the  credit  of 
the  whole.  But  a  very  substantial,  permanent,  and 
grateful  relief  can  be  afforded  to  the  States  by  reimburs- 
ing only  a  minor  fraction  of  their  expenditures;  and  this, 
in  the  judgment  of  the  committee,  can  be  done  without 
injuring  the  credit  of  the  Government  in  the  slightest  de- 
gree.    Indeed,  the  credit  of  the  Government  will  be  ma- 


Doc.  No.  12.  70 

terially  strengthened  by  any  prudent  measure  winch  will 
enable  the  States  to  provide  the  means  of  paving  their 
indebtedness,  and  thus  reducing  the  rate  of  local  and 
direct  taxation,  now  so  oppressively  high  throughout  the 

country. 

Influenced  by  these  considerations,  the  committee  havo 
agreed  to  report,  as  the  basis  of  reimbursement,  a  sum 
equivalent  to  twenty-five  per  cent,  of  the  average  ex- 
penditure throughout  the  loyal  States — in  other  words, 
fifty-five  dollars  for  each  man  furnished — service  being 
reduced  to  the  uniform  standard  of  three  years.  At  this 
rate  the  following  amounts  would  be  reimbursed  to  the 
several  States  : 

Maine $3,112,725 

New  Hampshire 1,695,485 

Vermont.    1,597,860 

Massachusetts , 6,811,420 

Rhode  Island 983,290 

Connecticut 2,778,270 

New  York 20,993,2S0 

New  Jersey 3,068,175 

Pennsylvania 14,715,690 

Delaware 566,665 

Maryland 2,238,060 

Carried  forward $58,560,920

It  is  not  proposed,  of  course,  to  pay  tins  amount  to  the 
States  hi  cash.  It  would  not  be  desirable,  even  if  it  were 
practicable,  to  make  the  payment  in  that  way.  The  mode 
©f  reimbursement  recommended  by  the  committee  is  to 
issue  bonds  of  the  United  States  to  the  several  States  for 
the  amounts  adjudged  to  be  due  them  ;  the  bonds  to  be 
registered,  to  be  redeemable  at  the  pleasure  of  the  United 
States  after  twenty  years  from  date,  and  to  bear  interest 
at  the  rate  of  five  per  cent,  per  annum,  payable  semi- 
annually in  lawful  money. 

And  in  issuing  bonds  for  this  purpose,  it  is  very  impor- 
tant for  the  interests  of  the  public  treasury  and  the  pro- 
tection of  the  public  credit,  that  the  States  should  not  be 
allowed  to  dispose  of  them  until  they  become  redeemable 
by  the  Government.  Hence  the  bill  submitted  expressly 
declares  that  the  bonds  to  be  issued  shall  not  be  nego- 
tiable until  after  the  1st  day  of  July,  a.  d.  1SS6,  and 
then  only  upon  the  indorsement  of  the  Governor  of  the 
State  to  which  the  bonds  may  belong.  And  it  is  respect- 
fully submitted  that  this  provision  is  as  much  for  the  ad- 
vantage of  the  States  as  for  the  General  Government, 
even  were  it  possible  that  their  interests  on  such  a 
question  could  be  antagonistic.  Such  a  restraint  on  the 
States  will,  with  certainty,  cause  the  bonds  to  be  used  as  a 
sinking  fund  for  the  redemption  of  whatever  State  debt 
may   exist,  and   will    effectually   prevent    their   sudden 


73  Doc.  No.  12. 

diversion  to  any  scheme  which  mature  reflection  might 
not  approve.  The  indorsement  of  the  Governor  being 
requisite  to  make  the  bonds  negotiable,  a  perfect  safe- 
guard is  thus  provided  against  any  fraudulent  use  of 
them  within  the  time  specified,  and  also  against  any  loss 
on  account  of  theft  or  accidental  destruction. 

The  committee  have  also  deemed  it  important  that 
each  State,  on  receiving  the  bonds,  shall  thereby  relin- 
quish all  further  claim  on  the  General  Government  for 
any  expenses  incurred  or  losses  sustained  during  the  late 
war,  either  by  the  State  or  by  any  municipal  corporation 
within  the  State.  The  claims  which  may  be  preferred 
are  endless  in  character  and  in  amount,  and  it  will  be  a 
great  point  gained  if  the  General  Government  can,  by  a 
comprehensive  payment  of  the  kind  now  recommended, 
at  once  and  finally  close  the  door  against  all  demands  for 
specific  appropriations  of  this  nature.  It  is  hazarding 
little  to  say  that,  in  this  view  alone,  the  measure  is  one  of 
wise  and  permanent  economy  to  the  General  Govern- 
ment. 

It  is  believed  that  the  proposed  measure  is  founded  on 
right  and  justice, because  all  expenditures  that  were  made 
to  preserve  the  life  of  the  nation  should,  as  far  as  practi- 
cable, be  borne  in  common  by  those  who  share  the 
benefits   and   blessings   of  our   Government.     It  would 


Doc.  No.  12.  74 

seem  flagrantly  unjust  to  leave  a  heavy  local  debt  on  a 
portion  of  the  States  when  that  debt  was  incurred  for  the 
common  benefit  of  all  the  States.  To  ask  that  the  General 
Government  should  refund  one-quarter  part  of  the  local 
expenditure  is  certainly  a  very  moderate  proposition,  and 
if  there  be  any  injustice  therein,  it  consists  in  not 
going  far  enough  in  the  direction  of  relief  to  the  loyal 
States. 

The  increase  to  the  national  debt  caused  by  this  reim- 
bursement is  nominal  rather  than  real.  It  does  not 
add  a  single  dollar  to  the  debt  of  the  country.  It  merely 
changes  the  form  of  a  certain  portion  of  that  debt  from  a 
State  and  local  to  a  national  and  general  obligation,  bear- 
ing impartially  on  all  the  States  and  on  all  the  people  of 
the  Union. 

The  General  Government  has  the  great  advantage  of 
monopolizing  all  the  channels  of  indirect  taxation,  leaving 
to  the  States  no  mode  of  raising  revenue  except  that  which 
13  the  hardest  and  most  oppressive.  And  the  direct  local 
tax  comes  with  all  the  more  severity  on  a  large  class  of 
the  community — especially  holders  of  real  estate — from 
the  fact  that  so  great  a  proportion  of  the  personal  prop- 
erty has  sought  investment  in  Government  bonds,  which 
are  expressly  exempt  from  State  and  municipal  taxa- 
tion. 


75  Doc.  No.  12. 

Considerations  of    this   character    have  had   a    largo 
influence  on  the  committee  in  proposing  the  measuro 
which,  with  these  explanations,  is  now  respectfully  sub 
mitted.

Doc.  No.  ]  2.  80 


A  BILL 

TO  REIMBURSE  THE  STATES  THAT  HAVE  FURNISHED  TROOPS  TO 
THE  UNION  ARMY,  FOR  ADVANCES  MADE  AND  EXPENSES  IN- 
CURRED IN  RAISING  THE  SAME. 

Whereas,  The  States  that  furnished  troops  to  the  Union 
army  during  the  late  war  were  subjected  to  very  heavy 
expenses,  amounting  in  the  aggregate  to  four  hundred 
and  seventy-live  million  dollars,  a  large  proportion  of 
which  has  assumed  the  form  of  oppressive  debt ;  and, 
whereas,  this  entire  outlay  was  made  for  the  common 
cause  of  the  Union,  and  therefore  constitutes  an  equit- 
able claim  on  the  common  treasury  of  the  nation; 
therefore, 

Be  it  enacted  by  the  Senate  and  House  of  Representatives 
of  the  United  States  of  America  in  Congress  assembled*  That 
there  shall  be  reimbursed  by  the  United  States  to  each  of 
the  States  that  famished  troops  to  the  Union  army,  and 
also  to  the  several  Territories  and  the  District  of  Colum- 
bia, a  sum  equal  to  fifty-five  dollars  for  each  man  duly 
enlisted  into  the  military  or  naval  service  of  the  United 
States  during  the  late  war,  the  total  number  being  reduced 
to  a  uniform  standard  of  three-years  service,  viz : 

To  the  State  of  Maine,  for  fifty-six  thousand  five  hun- 
dred and  ninety-live  men,  three  million  one  hundred  and 
twelve  thousand  seven  hundred  and  twenty-five  dollars. 


81  Doc.  No.  12. 

To  the  State  of  New  Hampshire,  for  thirty  thousand 
eight  hundred  and  twenty -seven  men,  one  million  six 
hundred  and  ninety-five  thousand  four  hundred  and 
eighty-five  dollars. 

To  the  State  of  Vermont,  for  twenty-nine  thousand  and 
fifty-two  men,  one  million  five  hundred  and  ninety-seven 
thousand  eight  hundred  and  sixty  dollars. 

To  the  State  of  Massachusetts,  for  one  hundred  and 
twenty-three  thousand  eight  hundred  and  forty-four  men, 
six  million  eight  hundred  and  eleven  thousand  four  hun- 
dred and  twenty  dollars. 

To  the  State  of  Rhode  Island,  for  seventeen  thousand 
eight  hundred  and  seventy-eight  men,  nine  hundred  and 
eighty-three  thousand  two  hundred  and  ninety  dollars. 

To  the  State  of  Connecticut,  for  fifty  thousand  rive  hun- 
dred and  fourteen  men,  two  million  seven  hundred  and 
seventy-eight  thousand  two  hundred  and  seventy  dollars.. 

To  the  State  of  New  York,  for  three  hundred  and 
eighty-one  thousand  six  hundred  and  ninety-six  men, 
twenty  million  nine  hundred  and  ninety-three  thousand 
two  hundred  and  eighty  dollars. 

To  the   State  of  New   Jersey,  for   fifty-five   thousand, 
seven  hundred  and  eighty-five  men,  three  million  sixty- 
eight  thousand  one  hundred  and  seventy-five  dollars. 
Vol.  II.— 6 


Doc.  No.  12.  82 

To  the  State  of  Pennsylvania,  for  two  hundred  and 
sixty-seven  thousand  fivu  hundred  and  fifty-eight  men, 
fourteen  million  seven  hundred  and  fifteen  thousand  six 
hundred  and  ninety  dollars. 

To  the  State  of  Delaware,  for  ten  thousand  three  hun- 
dred and  three  men,  five  hundred  and  sixty-six  thousand 
six  hundred  and  sixty-five  dollars. 

To  the  State  of  Maryland,  for  forty  thousand  six  hun- 
dred and  ninety-two  men,  two  million  two  hundred  and 
thirty-eight  thousand  and  sixty  dollars. 

To  the  State  of  West  Virginia,  for  twenty-seven  thou- 
sand six  hundred  and  fifty-three  men,  one  million  five 
hundred  and  twentv  thousand  nine  hundred  and  fifteen 
dollars. 

To  the  State  of  Ohio,  for  two  hundred  and  thirty-seven 
thousand  nine  hundred  and  seventy-six  men,  thirteen  mil- 
lion eighty-eight  thousand  six  hundred  and  eighty  dollars. 

To  the  State  of  Indiana,  for  one  hundred  and  fifty-two 
thousand  two  hundred  and  eighty-three  men,  eight  million 
three  hundred  and  seventy-five  thousand  five  hundred  and 
sixty-five  dollars. 

To  the  State  of  Illinois,  for  two  hundred  and  twelve

Sec.  2.  And  be  it  further  enacted,  That  the  amounts  to 
be  thus  reimbursed  shall  be  in  registered  bonds  of  the 
United  States,  of  not  less  than  one  thousand  dollars  each, 
bearing  interest  at  the  rate  of  five  per  centum  per  annum, 
payable  semi-annually  in  lawful  money,  and  redeemable 
at  the  pleasure  of  the  United  States,  after  twenty  years 
from  date.  Said  bonds  shall  be  dated  July  one,  eighteen 
hundred  and  sixty-six,  and  interest  thereafter  shall  be  pay- 
able on  the  first  day  of  January  and  first  day  of  July  each 
year ;  said  interest  to  be  payable  and  said  bonds  to  be  re- 
deemable out  of  moneys  to  be  hereafter  appropriated  by 
Congress. 


*oJ 


Sec  3.  And  be  it  farther  enacted,  That  each  bond  issued 
in  pursuance  of  this  act  shall  have  plainly  printed  or  en- 
graved thereon  the  words  following,  viz.,  ';  That  bonds  of 

which  this  is  one  are  issued  to  the  State  of in  full 

reimbursement  for  expenses  incurred  by  said  State  in  the 


Doc.  No.  12.  86 

war  for  the  Union.  Said  bonds  are  not  negotiable  until 
nftcr  the  first  day  of  July,  Anno  Domini  eighteen  hundred 
and  eighty-six,  and  then  only  upon  the  indorsement  of 

the  Governor  of  the  State.  And  said  bonds  are  accepted 
by  >aid  State  in  full  payment  of  all  claims  for  expenses 
incurred  or  losses  sustained  in  the  war  for  the  Union, 
either  by  the  State  or  by  any  municipal  corporation  within 
the  State." 

Sec.  4.  And  be  it  further  enacted,  That  the  bonds  au- 
thorized by  this  act  shall  not  be  delivered  to  any  State  until 
the  Legislature  thereof  lias  formally  consented  to  accept 
them  on  the  terms  contained  in  the  third  section,  and  upon 
such  consent  being  properly  certified  to  the  Secretary  of 
the  Treasury  by  the  Governor  of  any  State,  the  Secretary 
shall,  on  the  Governor's  receipt  therefor,  issue  to  such  State 
its  proper  amount  of  bonds,  as  provided  in  the  first  section 
of  this  act.  But  the  condition  contained  in  the  third  sec- 
tion shall  not  be  construed  to  exclude  any  demand  or 
claim  from  a  State  or  municipal  corporation  which  can 
be  audited  and  paid  under  any  law  in  force  at  the  time 
of  the  approval  of  this  act. 

Sec.  5.  And  be  it  farther  enacted,  That  the  Secretary  of 
State  shall  forward  to  the  Governor  of  each  State  a  certi- 
fied copy  of  this  act  within  thirty  days  from  the  date  of 
approval;  and  the  Secretary  of  the  Treasury  is  hereby 
charged  with  executing  the  provisions  of  this  act. 


APPENDIX    V. 


STATEMENT 

Showing  the  number  of  men  re-enlisted  in  the  field,  reported  from  the 
Adjutant-General's  office  at  Albany  to  the  "War  Department,  cred- 
ited to  the  County  of  New  York,  from  April,  1884,  to  April,  1865, 
showing  the  Eegiments  to  which  the  men  belonged  and  the  num- 
ber re-enlisting  in  each  Eegiment,  and  the  Districts  to  which  they 
were  severally  credited. 


D> 


w 


COMMUNICATION. 


General  Headquarters,  State  of  New  York, 
Adjutant-General's  Office, 

Albany,  October  2,  1865. 

Hon.  Orison  Blunt, 

New  York  City: 

Sir — I  have  the  honor  to  transmit  herewith  extracts 
from  the  reports  made  from  this  office  to  the  War  Depart 
mcnt  of  re-enlisted  men,  showing  the  number  of  men 
credited  to  the  City  of  New  York,  and  the  regiment  in 
which  they  re-enlisted.  No  report  of  this  class  of  credit? 
has  been  made  since  April  10,  1865. 

Very  respectfully, 

Your  obedient  servant, 

(Signed)  J.  B.  STONEHOUSE, 

Assistant  Adjutant- General,
